         <div class="readable stacked" id="description" style="right:0">
          <span id="freeTextContainer13067277259336677621">
           A thrillingly reimagined fairy tale from the truly magical combination of author Neil Gaiman and illustrator Chris Riddell  weaving together a sort-of Snow White and an almost Sleeping Beauty with a thread of dark magic, which will hold readers spellbound from start to finish.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           On the eve of her wedding, a young queen sets out to rescue a princess from an enchantment. She
          </span>
          <span id="freeText13067277259336677621" style="display:none">
           A thrillingly reimagined fairy tale from the truly magical combination of author Neil Gaiman and illustrator Chris Riddell  weaving together a sort-of Snow White and an almost Sleeping Beauty with a thread of dark magic, which will hold readers spellbound from start to finish.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           On the eve of her wedding, a young queen sets out to rescue a princess from an enchantment. She casts aside her fine wedding clothes, takes her chain mail and her sword and follows her brave dwarf retainers into the tunnels under the mountain towards the sleeping kingdom. This queen will decide her own future  and the princess who needs rescuing is not quite what she seems. Twisting together the familiar and the new, this perfectly delicious, captivating and darkly funny tale shows its creators at the peak of their talents.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Lavishly produced, packed with glorious Chris Riddell illustrations enhanced with metallic ink, this is a spectacular and magical gift.
          </span>
          <a data-text-id="13067277259336677621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
           ...more
          </a>

                   <span class="fullContent">
                    I have always believed you don't have to be a child to enjoy children's books. Especially when Neil Gaiman takes familiar tales and twists them around. Just buy it for yourself. It is exceedingly pretty, too. Chris Riddell's illustrations are marvelous.

              <div class="section firstReview">
               <div class="review" id="review_1085547809" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085547809" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19649406-lucy" title="Lucy">
                 <img alt="Lucy" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/users/1431159375p2/19649406.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085547809?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">
                   Nov 12, 2014
                  </a>
                  <a class="user" href="/user/show/19649406-lucy" title="Lucy">
                   Lucy
                  </a>
                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">
                   4 of 5 stars
                  </a>
                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19649406-lucy?shelf=2014">
                    2014
                   </a>
                   ,
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19649406-lucy?shelf=retellings">
                    retellings
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1085547809" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer2845295107891536858">
                    The first thing you should know: this is NOT a lesbian retelling of Sleeping Beauty. I'm sure you've all seen the Chris Riddell illustration of Snow White kissing Sleeping Beauty awake by now, and will have seen this book lauded as LGBT representation. It is not.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Suffice to say, I was let down. I was expecting a properly queer retelling and that's not what I got. What I got was one sweet lady smooch and one (admittedly beautiful) illustration to accompany it...and that was all. Literally. Not tru
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText2845295107891536858" style="display:none">
                    The first thing you should know: this is NOT a lesbian retelling of Sleeping Beauty. I'm sure you've all seen the Chris Riddell illustration of Snow White kissing Sleeping Beauty awake by now, and will have seen this book lauded as LGBT representation. It is not.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Suffice to say, I was let down. I was expecting a properly queer retelling and that's not what I got. What I got was one sweet lady smooch and one (admittedly beautiful) illustration to accompany it...and that was all. Literally. Not true love's kiss. Not anything's kiss. The kiss was as impersonal as bringing a clockwork automaton back to life by  winding its mechanism.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    I waited to give this book a rating because if I'd rated it as soon as I finished it would have only got two or three stars - that's how annoyed I was with it. However, I am bumping it up to four because for starters, nothing Neil Gaiman writes is ever BAD, Chris Riddell's illustrations are beautiful as usual and the production quality of the book is flawless. It is a VERY attractive book and the story itself is whimsical and lovely and filled with lots of amusing side characters, like all good fairy tales. Finally, I'm giving it four stars because there is a truly EPIC twist that I would have absolutely loved if I hadn't been so thirsty for proper lesbian representation.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    If the lack of proper queerness will not bother you, you will probably love this book. If you're looking for a book to be the answer to your lady-loving fairytale prayers, then this is not the book you're looking for. (And in that case, I recommend Ash by Malinda Lo, which is still not perfect but it's a damn sight better than this.)
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="2845295107891536858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>

                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_5" title="it was amazing">

                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18321322-sarah-churchill?shelf=books-i-own">

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1080245092" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer6680273412231884482">
                    This pair have never let me down yet.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The Sleeper and the Spindle is a fairytale retelling / mashup of Sleeping Beauty and Snow White, but with the characteristic darkness and twists we'd expect from Gaiman.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Riddell's illustrations are as stunning as always, presented in black, white and gold to give a very traditional and magical feel to a very modern fairytale.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    It's a short story, made to be read it one sitting, and I would say it's the perfect bedtime story if it wasn't for the extra level of
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText6680273412231884482" style="display:none">
                    This pair have never let me down yet.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The Sleeper and the Spindle is a fairytale retelling / mashup of Sleeping Beauty and Snow White, but with the characteristic darkness and twists we'd expect from Gaiman.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Riddell's illustrations are as stunning as always, presented in black, white and gold to give a very traditional and magical feel to a very modern fairytale.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    It's a short story, made to be read it one sitting, and I would say it's the perfect bedtime story if it wasn't for the extra level of unsettling Gaiman creepiness lathered on top. I guess it depends on the kid!
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    I loved it, I will read it again and again, studying the artwork in fine detail, and I'm very happy to have this is my collection.
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="6680273412231884482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>
                 </div>

                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fairytale">
                    fairytale

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1262318535" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer14923288476963546410">
                    <strong>
                     Spoilers
                    </strong>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Disappointing. The illustrations were great, the story on the other hand wasn't.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    I thought a mash up of Snow White and Sleeping Beauty would be interesting, that Snow White saving Sleeping Beauty would be a fresh and exciting twist on things. Unfortunately, even though Snow White saved the day (instead of being the usual damsel-in-distress) and Sleeping Beauty turned out to be a villain, it still somehow managed to read as stale, predictable and unoriginal.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Most of the book was spent on S
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText14923288476963546410" style="display:none">
                    <strong>
                     Spoilers
                    </strong>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Disappointing. The illustrations were great, the story on the other hand wasn't.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    I thought a mash up of Snow White and Sleeping Beauty would be interesting, that Snow White saving Sleeping Beauty would be a fresh and exciting twist on things. Unfortunately, even though Snow White saved the day (instead of being the usual damsel-in-distress) and Sleeping Beauty turned out to be a villain, it still somehow managed to read as stale, predictable and unoriginal.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Most of the book was spent on Snow White and her dwarves travelling from her kingdom to Sleeping Beauty's. It wasn't enjoyable or very gripping, there was no tension, no whimsy, no nothing. It was just flat, the only part I liked was at the end when Snow White ditched her fianc and her inevitable life of misery and oppression, and decided to travel elsewhere.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    If it wasn't for the artwork I'm not sure I would have bothered to finish it, I only kept reading just to see all the intricate and beautiful drawings.
                    <br/>
                   </span>

                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1085421507" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer8720984459990687910">
                    Preordered this as soon as I realized Book Depository had this UK edition. It's SOOO beautiful! The dust jacket is partially see through to the drawing underneath, and the entire book is beautifully illustrated. Every page takes a while just to absorb every detail. Chris Riddell is an incredible artist. The story itself spins a couple of well known fairy tales together in an interesting way, and only takes about an hour to go through.
                   </span>
                  </span>

              <div class="section">
               <div class="review" id="review_1247278034" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1247278034" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote" title="Sam Quixote">
                 <img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/users/1414622451p2/5759543.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1247278034?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">
                   Apr 06, 2015
                  </a>
                  <a class="user" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote" title="Sam Quixote">
                   Sam Quixote
                  </a>
                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_2" title="it was ok">
                   2 of 5 stars
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1247278034" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer15304632722545314620">
                    The Sleeper and the Spindle is an illustrated short story, mashing up Snow White and Sleeping Beauty with a feminist twist - the Prince Charming character is a woman and, gasp, she kisses another woman to awaken her! Also, most of the book is characters walking across a fantasy landscape so if youre a Tolkien fan, youre gonna love this!
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Are we still not over post-modern takes on fairy tales? Do we really need another darker version of a well-known, heavily Disneyfied story? Apparently Neil G
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText15304632722545314620" style="display:none">
                    The Sleeper and the Spindle is an illustrated short story, mashing up Snow White and Sleeping Beauty with a feminist twist - the Prince Charming character is a woman and, gasp, she kisses another woman to awaken her! Also, most of the book is characters walking across a fantasy landscape so if youre a Tolkien fan, youre gonna love this!
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Are we still not over post-modern takes on fairy tales? Do we really need another darker version of a well-known, heavily Disneyfied story? Apparently Neil Gaiman fans arent so the author reworks the stories to be female empowering because hes a savvy businessman who knows a major chunk of his audience is made up of women.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Thats probably me being cynical as Im sure this is a story Gaimans been dying to tell. Hey, it could be! Really, I just dont much care for his writing style. Its plodding, oh so bloody plodding, and the story isnt even that complex - a woman in armour and a trio of dwarfs go to a sleeping woman in a castle!
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Its 60-ish pages with lots of drawings to fill it out to that length and yet this book somehow feels even longer. Its basically all about the sleeper awakening at the end because thats when interesting things start happening, eclipsing the nothing and even more nothing that took place before.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Chris Riddells art is fine and his drawings are presented in black, white and gold, which is an unusual but good choice. Except none of his drawings are particularly memorable or unique so I wouldnt say the art stood out.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    I know fairy tales were originally much darker than most people realise, and thats what Gaimans going for, a kind of callback to those days while also mixing in progressive elements too. Alright, cool. But reading it is quite tedious as Gaimans taken a simple story and padded the hell out of it with lengthy descriptions of landscapes, objects - all kinds of things I forgot as soon as I read them - and average drawings.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Gaiman fans will eat The Sleeper and the Spindle up because its more of the same stuff he always churns out. I felt very meh about this pedestrian reimagining of some old stories.
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="15304632722545314620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>
                 </div>

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1085215880" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer10802639638352794702">
                    For the first time ever I like a Neil Gaiman novel. I am shocked. Shocked, I tell you.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <img alt="" class="escapedImg" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420921345r/13291665._SX540_.jpg" width="350"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    It wasn't until I came across a
                    <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/booksblog/2014/oct/16/neil-gaiman-russell-brand-modern-fairytale-makeover-princess" rel="nofollow">
                     Guardian article
                    </a>
                    with the above image that I decided to give Gaiman a another chance. I mean, how bad could a feminist retelling of Sleeping Beauty be? Besides, the library had a copy so only an investment of time would be required.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    A post-curse Snow White is a warrior queen about to get married to a seemingly inferior and submissive man she does not love. When the dwarfs report t
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText10802639638352794702" style="display:none">
                    For the first time ever I like a Neil Gaiman novel. I am shocked. Shocked, I tell you.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <img alt="" class="escapedImg" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420921345r/13291665._SX540_.jpg" width="350"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    It wasn't until I came across a
                    <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/booksblog/2014/oct/16/neil-gaiman-russell-brand-modern-fairytale-makeover-princess" rel="nofollow">
                     Guardian article
                    </a>
                    with the above image that I decided to give Gaiman a another chance. I mean, how bad could a feminist retelling of Sleeping Beauty be? Besides, the library had a copy so only an investment of time would be required.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    A post-curse Snow White is a warrior queen about to get married to a seemingly inferior and submissive man she does not love. When the dwarfs report that the Sleeping Beauty curse is spreading rapidly into Snow White's lands she jumps at the chance to leave and attempt to break it despite the many princes and knights who've died trying over the years.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    It's only when she and the dwarfs arrive at the castle that Gaiman's story really sets itself apart from other fairy tales and their retellings. Zombie-like sleepwalkers bent on killing. An elderly (and tragic) lady guardian and a Sleeping Beauty who aren't what you expect. A chaste kiss between Snow White and Sleeping Beauty to break the curse. And an ending which didn't feel quite right.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Instead of returning home, Snow White runs away from her royal responsibilities and her groom to travel with the dwarfs. Why not return home and refuse to marry? And abdicate the throne, if she really doesn't want to be queen? That takes more strength than running.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Everything I've read by Gaiman (his children's books) have received no more than two stars. Though he has intriguing ideas, his execution of them is poor, rarely gripping, and written in too few pages to do them justice. Bland characters I felt little for, one way or the other, is another common complaint. But yes, I had similar issues with
                    <em>
                     The Sleeper and the Spindle
                    </em>
                    . They weren't as pronounced this time. It's the unexpected and feminist twists that really sets this one apart. Black, white and gold illustrations were also positives I enjoyed.
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="10802639638352794702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>
                 </div>

              <div class="section">
               <div class="review" id="review_1079215561" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1079215561" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20383532-wolfsbane" title="Wolfsbane">
                 <img alt="Wolfsbane" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/users/1369323421p2/20383532.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1079215561?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">
                   Oct 13, 2014
                  </a>
                  <a class="user" href="/user/show/20383532-wolfsbane" title="Wolfsbane">
                   Wolfsbane
                  </a>
                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_2" title="it was ok">
                   2 of 5 stars
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1079215561" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer1958188632497016061">
                    I know I am probably going to attract a lot of animosity with this review, but I can't help feeling a bit cheated.
                    <br/>
                    I defended the emotionally raw, jump in the dark that was The Ocean at the End of the Lane, because it was so cathartic, and new, a whole new take on the novel, the person, all in all so authentic.
                    <br/>
                    Maybe it is because, like many people, I have read all of his works from the beginning, but I could see just where this was going from the start. And I just felt like it was the kind of bi
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText1958188632497016061" style="display:none">
                    I know I am probably going to attract a lot of animosity with this review, but I can't help feeling a bit cheated.
                    <br/>
                    I defended the emotionally raw, jump in the dark that was The Ocean at the End of the Lane, because it was so cathartic, and new, a whole new take on the novel, the person, all in all so authentic.
                    <br/>
                    Maybe it is because, like many people, I have read all of his works from the beginning, but I could see just where this was going from the start. And I just felt like it was the kind of biscuit you give a child to keep him quiet. Only I am 30 and I need a bit more than that. Maybe a cake, or a treacle tart.
                    <br/>
                    That said, nothing wrong with the writing itself and the illustrations are mesmerizing.
                    <br/>
                    Anyway, this is just an opinion. Personal opinion. Mine. Not trying to make anyone angry.
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="1958188632497016061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">

              <div class="section">
               <div class="review" id="review_1100990042" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100990042" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nikki" title="Nikki">
                 <img alt="Nikki" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1100990042?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">
                   Nov 08, 2014
                  </a>
                  <a class="user" href="/user/show/223837-nikki" title="Nikki">
                   Nikki
                  </a>
                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">
                   4 of 5 stars
                  </a>
                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nikki?shelf=artwork">
                    artwork
                   </a>
                   ,
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nikki?shelf=fairytales">
                    fairytales
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1100990042" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer2865906159193006096">
                    <em>
                     The Sleeper and the Spindle
                    </em>
                    is a gorgeous book: the illustrations are all in black and gold, and there are some really beautiful pages. Riddell was just the right illustrator to bring the story to life, I think. The copy I have is really great: the dust cover is transparent, with the pattern of roses on it; the cover of the book itself is the sleeping woman.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    If you know Neil Gaiman's work, the rest of this is perhaps not surprising. It takes both Snow White and Sleeping Beauty, and puts them in a
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText2865906159193006096" style="display:none">
                    <em>
                     The Sleeper and the Spindle
                    </em>
                    is a gorgeous book: the illustrations are all in black and gold, and there are some really beautiful pages. Riddell was just the right illustrator to bring the story to life, I think. The copy I have is really great: the dust cover is transparent, with the pattern of roses on it; the cover of the book itself is the sleeping woman.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    If you know Neil Gaiman's work, the rest of this is perhaps not surprising. It takes both Snow White and Sleeping Beauty, and puts them in a unified world that is a little darker, a little different, a little more mature than the sanitised stories we see so much of now. This ain't Disney. It's still a fairytale, but it's something different, too -- something a little bit creepy, even.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The LGBT representation that I have seen this book being lauded for is... not exactly. There's one kiss which appears to be so if you see the illustration on its own -- and it's a gorgeous illustration -- but it doesn't mean what it seems to mean, in context. Which is a little bit of a cop-out, really, since there's excitement around this book on the back of it.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    But really, romance isn't at the heart of this fairytale. A search for autonomy is really what's going on; a shrugging away from the familiar fairytale 'happy ever after'.
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="2865906159193006096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>
                 </div>

              <div class="section">
               <div class="review" id="review_1166739725" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166739725" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7716112-dylan" title="Dylan">

                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

                   Jan 13, 2015
                  </a>
                  <a class="user" href="/user/show/7716112-dylan" title="Dylan">
                   Dylan
                  </a>
                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">
                   4 of 5 stars
                  </a>
                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7716112-dylan?shelf=books-i-own">
                    books-i-own
                   </a>
                   ,
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7716112-dylan?shelf=read-2015">
                    read-2015
                   </a>

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1166739725" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer5327847170605259293">
                    This book is just absolutely stunning! Like I'm just...
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421162665ra/13331685.gif"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The cover is beautiful, and I love that it has a partially transparent dust jacket, to see the sleeper underneath.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The illustrations in the book are also quite beautiful. There is a limited colour palette of black, white and gold. This really allowed the artist to focus on detail, and also the characters. Which were both very well done.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The story is a fairytale retelling combining Sleeping Beauty and Snow White. I really enjoyed the way it was
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText5327847170605259293" style="display:none">
                    This book is just absolutely stunning! Like I'm just...
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421162665ra/13331685.gif"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The cover is beautiful, and I love that it has a partially transparent dust jacket, to see the sleeper underneath.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The illustrations in the book are also quite beautiful. There is a limited colour palette of black, white and gold. This really allowed the artist to focus on detail, and also the characters. Which were both very well done.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The story is a fairytale retelling combining Sleeping Beauty and Snow White. I really enjoyed the way it was adapted, and the twists as well as the overall plot.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The one thing that was missing for me though, was depth. I felt like the characters and the plot, were very on the surface. I didn't expect to dive into multidimensional characters, and swim in rich story lines. But I needed a bit more to grip me, and make me connect to the story. I enjoyed the reading experience, but no more than that.
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="5327847170605259293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1092968635" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer13979927880635832905">
                    Neil Gaiman is quickly becoming one of my favourite writers, more so his children/YA books than his adult books. Recently, I've even started reading his graphic novels, something I probably should have done years ago as I've come to realize how absolutely fantastic they are!
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    This one is no different, as he brings to life two fairytales and combines them effortlessly that you don't see it coming. Intertwining different aspects of Snow White with Sleeping Beauty, he takes you on a journey that is n
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText13979927880635832905" style="display:none">
                    Neil Gaiman is quickly becoming one of my favourite writers, more so his children/YA books than his adult books. Recently, I've even started reading his graphic novels, something I probably should have done years ago as I've come to realize how absolutely fantastic they are!
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    This one is no different, as he brings to life two fairytales and combines them effortlessly that you don't see it coming. Intertwining different aspects of Snow White with Sleeping Beauty, he takes you on a journey that is new and into uncharted territory, in the process creating a completely new story. I loved the twists and turns, I love the unpredictable ending and the creepiness of it all.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    I've already ordered Hansel and Gretel, and I'm sure to expect a lot of new twists added to that fairytale. Can't wait.
                   </span>

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1087640490" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer3978636124413792164">
                    Gaaaaaaah! So here I am, having decided that I'm definitely not reading any more remixed fairytales, because in 90% of cases, they turn out to be overrated and rarely ever seem to be adding anything genuinely new, so usually you just get a thinly remodelled, slightly-repackaged-but-with-same-old-content yawnfest. And then of course along comes Neil Gaiman and basically goes, "Hm, I could do this one thing that's been done to death by everyone and their aunt, only I could, y'know, make it AWESOME
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText3978636124413792164" style="display:none">
                    Gaaaaaaah! So here I am, having decided that I'm definitely not reading any more remixed fairytales, because in 90% of cases, they turn out to be overrated and rarely ever seem to be adding anything genuinely new, so usually you just get a thinly remodelled, slightly-repackaged-but-with-same-old-content yawnfest. And then of course along comes Neil Gaiman and basically goes, "Hm, I could do this one thing that's been done to death by everyone and their aunt, only I could, y'know, make it AWESOME,
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    a.k.a.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <img class="escapedImg" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415061431r/11720828.jpg"/>
                    ,
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    and then of COURSE I have to read it, and of COURSE it's bloody unique and bloody brilliant, and the edition itself is all ridiculously gorgeous.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Life is hard, people.
                   </span>

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1265548829" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer8555331763507820572">
                    What a gorgeous little book! Gaiman and Riddell = the dream team, and I hope that they are already working on their next book together. The illustrations are sooooo beautiful and I enjoyed Gaiman's take on this classic fairytale. I really wish it was longer though. I think that this version had all the potential to become a full-blown tale of epic awesomeness but now it left me wanting a bit more.
                   </span>
                  </span>

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1314307427" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer16664778472882033736">
                    The Sleeper and the Spindle really is a tale worth investing in. There is twist upon twist, a hint of true fairytale darkness and a long-awaited and very much-discussed (online at least) kiss. Even without the story this book is lovely  translucent hardcover, with lavish, gilded illustrations throughout, including illuminated letters and double-page spreads redrawing quotes from the neighboring text.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    I have to admit a bias here (is it obvious?) as Chris Riddell is possibly (is
                    <em>
                     definitely
                    </em>
                    ) my fav
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText16664778472882033736" style="display:none">
                    The Sleeper and the Spindle really is a tale worth investing in. There is twist upon twist, a hint of true fairytale darkness and a long-awaited and very much-discussed (online at least) kiss. Even without the story this book is lovely  translucent hardcover, with lavish, gilded illustrations throughout, including illuminated letters and double-page spreads redrawing quotes from the neighboring text.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    I have to admit a bias here (is it obvious?) as Chris Riddell is possibly (is
                    <em>
                     definitely
                    </em>
                    ) my favourite illustrator, ever. I have been fascinated by his distinctive, stunning illustrations since I first stumbled across the excellent Edge Chronicles as a child. His ink-sketched characters bring any words to life, and though Neil Gaimans words are so skillful they never really need illustration, Gaiman and Riddell are a match made in heaven  or, more likely, one of the fantastical worlds these creative geniuses inhabit.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <a href="http://www.nzbooklovers.co.nz/uncategorized/the-sleeper-and-the-spindle-by-neil-gaiman-chris-riddell/" rel="nofollow">
                     Full review here
                    </a>
                   </span>

                    ...more
                   </a>

               <div class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1228778852" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228778852" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/808316-priyanka" title="Priyanka">
                 <img alt="Priyanka" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/users/1431057466p2/808316.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1228778852?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">
                   Mar 17, 2015
                  </a>
                  <a class="user" href="/user/show/808316-priyanka" title="Priyanka">
                   Priyanka
                  </a>
                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">
                   4 of 5 stars
                  </a>
                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/808316-priyanka?shelf=short-stories">
                    short-stories
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1228778852" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer33176618713988638">
                    Every once in a while a story comes along that doesn't exactly retell one or more fairy tales, but instead creates a new kind of fairy tale that is firmly rooted in the fairy tales of old. The Sleeper and the Spindle is one such story; something of a work of art, and a thing to treasure, made even better by its gorgeous illustrations by Chris Riddell.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    An enchanting and timeless piece, inspired by both Snow White and Sleeping Beauty, this is an empowering tale of terror, courage and tragedy. Famil
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText33176618713988638" style="display:none">
                    Every once in a while a story comes along that doesn't exactly retell one or more fairy tales, but instead creates a new kind of fairy tale that is firmly rooted in the fairy tales of old. The Sleeper and the Spindle is one such story; something of a work of art, and a thing to treasure, made even better by its gorgeous illustrations by Chris Riddell.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    An enchanting and timeless piece, inspired by both Snow White and Sleeping Beauty, this is an empowering tale of terror, courage and tragedy. Familiar bits of both these traditional tales have been twisted around with women as warrior queens and unexpected malefactors - beautiful people doing ugly things.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Well-nigh Sleeping Beauty and a kind of Snow White are combined in a way that only Gaiman can, with a voice so unique  funny, wise and engaging.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    When fairy tales get the Neil Gaiman treatment, whats not to love about it!
                    <br/>
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="33176618713988638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>

                    First of all, this book is a beautiful piece of art. The cover and the illustrations are just stunning! The inside however did not blow me away as much as I hoped it would, but over all I liked it.
                    <br/>
                    I like how original the story is and I very much like the modern take on a classic fairytale, and I love the little twist at the end.                    </span>
                   <span id="freeText6211456351660221428" style="display:none">
                    First of all, this book is a beautiful piece of art. The cover and the illustrations are just stunning! The inside however did not blow me away as much as I hoped it would, but over all I liked it.
                    <br/>
                    I like how original the story is and I very much like the modern take on a classic fairytale, and I love the little twist at the end. The backside is that I felt a lack of details and I wanted more information surrounding The Queen and her past. Maybe we can hope for a prequel of some sort? Or just more books in this world, re-telling other fairytales?

              <div class="section">
               <div class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1294589574" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1294589574" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21724441-eveymorgan" title="Eveymorgan">
                 <img alt="Eveymorgan" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/users/1372417805p2/21724441.jpg"/>

                    The best thing about this was the illustrations. It was just gorgeous. The layout, the colouring, it was all done magnificently. It was a wonderful book to read.                    </span>
                   <span id="freeText14693976391051268543" style="display:none">
                    The best thing about this was the illustrations. It was just gorgeous. The layout, the colouring, it was all done magnificently. It was a wonderful book to read. I must admit I was a little disappointed by the story. First of all I had heard it was a queer retelling of the story, with big pictures of the two women kissing in articles promoting the book. Alas this was not the case. Also it was quite disappointing to see that while the queen put on her armour and sword, she never actually got to fight anything but spent her entire time running away. It wasn't very heroic. Though the ending with the magical twist was really good and I liked that a lot. I'm glad I got a copy even though I didn't like it as much as I was hoping.

The cover itself is spectacular and I'm really fond of the transparent jacket that gives a layered effect to the surface. Although the story is straightforward and is really just a children's bedtime story, Gaiman litters it with little hidden gems for adults to discover and probably saves their sanity in the meantime.

             <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
              <div class="section">
               <div class="review" id="review_1220148465" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1220148465" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8943949-charlotte-jones" title="Charlotte Jones">
                 <img alt="Charlotte Jones" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/users/1361900141p2/8943949.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1220148465?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate">
                   Mar 08, 2015
                  </a>
                  <a class="user" href="/user/show/8943949-charlotte-jones" title="Charlotte Jones">
                   Charlotte Jones
                  </a>
                  rated it
                  <a class=" staticStars stars_4" title="really liked it">
                   4 of 5 stars
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1220148465" style="">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer10865995139269339971">
                    When I went to the Neil Gaiman talk in Liverpool, I had to buy one of the signed books that were on sale so I picked up The Sleeper and the Spindle, a dark fairy tale retelling by Neil Gaiman, illustrated by my favourite illustrator Chris Riddell.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Firstly, the book itself is gorgeous; the black and white illustrations have a hint of gold in places that just makes it feel like a luxurious book, the vellum overlay on the cover adds to this feeling as well, and the full page spreads just suck you in
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText10865995139269339971" style="display:none">
                    When I went to the Neil Gaiman talk in Liverpool, I had to buy one of the signed books that were on sale so I picked up The Sleeper and the Spindle, a dark fairy tale retelling by Neil Gaiman, illustrated by my favourite illustrator Chris Riddell.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Firstly, the book itself is gorgeous; the black and white illustrations have a hint of gold in places that just makes it feel like a luxurious book, the vellum overlay on the cover adds to this feeling as well, and the full page spreads just suck you into the story with the immense amount of detail packed in.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The story itself was fun, combining Sleeping Beauty and Snow White. I liked how their was a female heroine instead of the typical Prince Charming and also the twist towards the end. However, I do feel like the story jumped about quite a bit and I would have preferred it to be longer, but I understand that it is a childrens book so this is to be expected. I really loved reading this and its definitely something I will pick up again, even if it is just to browse through the beautiful illustrations.
                   </span>
                   <a data-text-id="10865995139269339971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">
                    ...more
                   </a>
                  </span>
                 </div>

                function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NQ+IADQIAK1TCcAcCrxGJuXM89aEFdP8yxaNYFEs83sm/+Kqqq5pZ8z/JvlfYLdvQte8IrRZ/XYedPdTqTY8Wg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1/m/f9GLxrFvD7qjTUoxW0eg/e+kCktMa94YjBhgMuXECdXVTy2ve/D5XEYYlsAS4LuyG5RGZca+vGK/4Hr9xA==')})
  }

Authors central to the&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText13049585196825745629\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;The Victorian fascination with fairyland is reflected in the literature of the period, which includes some of the most imaginative fairy tales ever written. They offer the shortest path to the age\'s dreams, desires, and wishes. Authors central to the nineteenth-century canon such as Thackeray, Oscar Wilde, Ford Madox Ford, and Rudyard Kipling wrote fairy tales, and authors primarily famous for their work in the genre include George MacDonald, Juliana Ewing, Mary De Morgan, and Andrew Lang. This anthology brings together fourteen of the best stories, by these and other outstanding practitioners, to show the vibrancy and variety of the form and its ability to reflect our deepest concerns.\n\nThe stories in this selection range from pure whimsy and romance to witty satire and darker, uncanny mystery. Paradox proves central to a form offered equally to children and adults. Fairyland is a dynamic and beguiling place, one that permits the most striking explorations of gender, suffering, love, family, and the travails of identity. Michael Newton\'s introduction and notes explore the literary marketplace in which these tales appeared, as well as the role they played in contemporary debates on scepticism and belief. The book also includes a selection of original illustrations by some of the masters of the field such as Richard Doyle, Arthur Hughes, and Walter Crane.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a
